As with most driers these days, this one has three heat settings plus a cold blast button and two speeds, high and low. It comes with two air \\"concentrators\\" as well as a few directions on how to style hair. Although this Conair is somewhat heavy and large, it's not as bulky as other large driers, another bonus. I keep my hair drier in a drawer, and my selection is often limited by what can fit inside since so many have bulbous housings. At 3 5/8 inches at its widest, this one just clears the drawer. It has a removable filter to clean out the lint that accumulates over time and which can decrease the life of a hair drier. The power cord is 6 feet long; unlike other models, this one does not have a retractable cord, something I don't care about but others may, given how long the cord is. This drier does not have a switch to convert to the greater European voltage standard. Americans who take their hair driers abroad will still have to use a converter and adapter sequence to use it. Because this isn't intended to be a portable appliance, this last omission should affect few people.<br /><br />I never thought I' could get this excited about a hair drier, but I really love it. I just hope it lasts a long time, as the company claims.<br /><br />-- Debbie Lee Wesselmann

Finally, I pulled the trigger and ordered this one, since the reviews seemed slightly better than the Infiniti 223X. I was really skeptical that it would be any better than my old dryer, but I AM SO GLAD I order this! This dryer is nothing short of astounding, and I can't believe I paid only $30 for it. Let me break this down: PROS: (1) SO POWERFUL. Although it is an 1875-watt model like my previous dryer, the airflow coming out of this feels twice as strong, no exaggeration. I feel like I'm in a wind tunnel when it's on High. (2) Accurate heat settings: The warm is a true warm, and the hot is a true hot, but not too hot as to unnecessarily damage your hair. (3) A Cool button that works instantly: I've never had a dryer whose Cool button actually shot out cool air quickly. The ability to switch from hot to cool in seconds really helps hold your style, especially if you are drying your hair with a round brush. This one just works like it should. (4) Lightweight: The people on here who complain about the weight baffle me. Have they ever used a dryer? I weighed this dryer and my old dryer on my kitchen scale and this one is much lighter. It's easy to hold and use for the duration of drying your hair. (5) Dries your hair fast: No exaggerating, this cut my dry time almost in half. The extra power and the accurate heat settings really make a difference. (6)Great results: My hair is soft, shiny, and styled as I desired. I thought the faster drying time might make it look more damaged but the opposite seems to be true. (7) Long cord. This is a really nice feature if you dry your hair in a room with plugs in inconvenient locations. CONS: (1) It's slightly louder than my old dryer, which seemed to produce an average amount of noise. I've never had a truly quiet dryer so I don't care that this thing is slightly louder. (2) No cord keeper. This, again, is a very minor complaint. In an ideal world this dryer would have one, but it's not a big deal. In sum: I simply don't see how anyone would regret purchasing this dryer. I have long, layered, average thickness hair that always seems difficult to dry. But since I got this dryer, it's been so much easier, faster, and the results are exactly what I want. I just hope it is durable. It feels like an absolute tank, but I'll report back in a few months.

  174. I considered a T3 but, the more reviews I read I began thinking, maybe I really don't need to spend that much. Plus, some of these dryer reviews stated the dryer would burn out, even the expensive ones. I saw some good reviews on a particular Revlon and some Conairs. My previous hair dryer (Pilmatic 2000) which is a professional version of Conair (from Sallys) had lasted about 7 years. One day it made a high pitch squeal and seemed to lose some of its power. It still worked but not as good, so I decided it was time.<br />On the description for this dryer stated it was an \\"AC\\" powered motor and I wondered what's that about? Googled and found an interesting explanation of AC vs. DC motors. AC Motors: larger, heavier, but less noisy, more durable. They operate on lower RPMs, which results in less stress put on the moving parts. This leads to a longer lifespan and less risk of breaking down or burning out. Typically AC hair dryers blow stronger than DC dryers. DC Motors: Blow dryer is much smaller, lighter, reach high speeds very quickly, and produce greater airflow for quicker drying. Since they run at higher RPMs, DC motors tend not to last as long and individual pieces of the dryer are subject to wear. In other words, you have to pick your poison and decide which features are most important to you, b/c you can't have it all. I like the price of this one; I don't have to always have the latest and greatest (at least with a blow dryer) and I don't want to go shopping again in a year for a new one. I knew I wanted Ionic and Tourmaline as I live in humid FL- this one had these options. Also, based on the description of different motors, I assumed my old dryer was an AC motor. I had been overall pleased with my old dryer so I purchased this one.<br />My hair is straight & my strands are fine in diameter; I have a lot of them so I would describe my hair as thick. The drying time has probably been cut in half as it was taking me around 20 minutes (when my olddryer was working properly). I actually have to be a bit careful b/c the straightening effect of the 'Ion' can make my hair kind of flat. However, I am compensating by using a little bit of a scrunching technique or I let my hair air dry a bit more and do other things in my morning routine first (because now I don't have to worry about any little frizzies my hair gets from air drying, b/c the Ion's from the dryer will take it out when I finish up w/ the dryer). I do recommend this dryer; it appears to be around the same quality of my old dryer and I suspect will last just as long. Also, the hook is not visible in the pic but there is one. In addition, I do not have a lot of upper body strength and I do not find the dryer too heavy. It is actually lighter than my old one. Also, the cord on this dryer is a bit shorter, it is about six feet long, my old dryer's cord was crazy long. But I will live with that.

  254. I have always found it difficult in the past when I needed to replace a hair dryer. The Infiniti Pro 1875 (model 259) clearly stands at the top of the list of quality hair dryers. My objectives were to find a heavy duty dryer that would last, but that didn't weigh a ton and had flexible settings that allowed me to find what worked best for me. While the Ininiti Pro isn't light, I find that it is ergonomically designed so that the weight is distributed and it doesn't feel that heavy to me. It is not quiet, but even on high speeds the sound is a smoother less irritating sound than most of the large hair dryers I have used in the past. The motor just sounds high quality rather than that high pitched irritating noise you get with a lot of dryers. It is true that it only has two speeds (Low and High), but the low speed is equivalent to medium on most dryers so unless a very low speed is necessary for you, I think you will find that the two speeds will meet your needs. One of the things that I hated about my past hair dryers was that you either burned your scalp or it was too cold to do much good. I don't even use the \\"hot\\" setting on this dryer. The warm with the low fan setting provides all of the drying power I need.<br /><br />Although you don't (hopefully) replace hair dryers all that often, it is worth taking some extra time to evaluate before you purchase. This is the first time I have actually been totally satisfied with a hair dryer and my sense is that the Ininiti Pro is solidly made and will last a long time. It is not the cheapest hair dryer you can buy, but considering the high quality, it is very reasonably priced.
  255. Bought this to replace a Revlon Tourmaline Ionic hairdryer that was frying my hair.<br /><br />Style wise, this rocks! It's a beautiful bright burnt orange. I like the placement on the buttons being centered on the inside of the handle - it works well for lefties or righties. I like the distinct temperature levels and the output of the dryer. The ONLY fault I have is that it is obscenely heavy. If you have joint pain or fibromyalgia - you may have to pass on this unit. I find that my arms fatigue halfway through doing my hair. It's easily twice the weight of my Revlon unit.
  256. This is a great product, and it dries my hair really well. I have had issues with other hair dryers sucking my hair in through the back and snagging it, but I have never had that problem with this one. It also has a really sleek design and a pretty color.<br /><br />It is kind of heavy compared to my old hair dryer, but you get used to it.

  258. I wanted a new ionic drier for our kids that wasn't as loud as our traditional hair drier. I got this one for the reviews on the powerful drying. Everyone's reviews said this was not very quiet, but I ordered it as ours was already very loud, so I figured I'd give it a shot. It turns out that this is indeed loud, but it actually lacks the high pitched squeal that you get from normal hair dryers. The is loud because of the low motor noise mixed with the amount of air that is being pushed out. Air can be pretty loud!!! Because it doesn't have the squeal that I hate, I can actually talk while using it, loudly, but it really is much better than the old one!
  259. Best hair dryer I've ever owned and I have owned quite a few in a wide price range. This beat a high end designer type hair dryer I owned hands down! This hair dryer is not light but not so heavy as to be cumbersome or unmanageable. I'm 64 years old and have no difficulty manipulating it. It's also as noisy as any other hair dryer but then again you won't be using it as long as most other air dryers as it really does dry hair faster. It's interesting because there is a silky quality to the air it blows out ( the ionic effect? ) and that same silky quality translates to the hair. My hair feels great, looks shiny and bouncy. I have a daughter who will definitely want to share this...I very infrequently write a review but wanted to let others know what a great product this is as I have depended on other's reviews in the past when deciding on a purchase.
